Yes, starting your day with good stretching is important to avoid work related MSK injuries. Nice Job! What do you need to do next? Return to [[option1]] Ergonomics is very important because we want to avoid injuries. There are several things we can do to help our bodies. [[chair]] [[scan bed]] [[ultrasound machine]] Return to [[option1]]<img src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d5/Xomed_ENTroll_Chair-_Ergonomic_surgical_chair%2C_Xomed.png"> Adjusting the scan ultrasound chair is important to do for each ultrasound exam and for technologist. By using good ergonomics, we can keep our bodies healthy. * Increase/decrease chair height * Lock/unlock the seat back * Move your seat forward/backward Return to [[set your machine & chair to optomize ergonomics]] <img src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a2/Captive%27s_medical_clinic%2C_Camp_6%2C_Guantanamo.jpg"> Adjusting the scan bed is important and there are several things we can do to ensure good ergonomics. * Increase/decrease bed height * Tilt your bed into needed position (Trendelenburg, Fowlers, etc.) * Raise/lower the bed rails Return to [[set your machine & chair to optomize ergonomics]] <img src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/Medical_ultrasound_examination.JPG"> Adjusting the ultrasound machine is important and there are several things we can do to ensure good ergonomics. The machine is adjusted for each sonographer and each examination you are completing. * Raise/lower your monitor so it is at comfortable height * Raise/lower your keyboard so it is at a comfortable height * Twist your base to match your desired scanning preference Return to [[set your machine & chair to optomize ergonomics]] <img src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d7/Questionnaire-checklist-completed.png"> The scanning protocols are essentially universal as established by the American College of Radiology (ACR). Some facilities might ask for a few more/less images. If you are ever unsure of what images to take and what order, please refer to these protocols. Return to [[option2]] <img src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c2/Abdominal_Ultrasound_General_Illustration.jpg"> In medical imaging, everything is based off knowing your normal anatomy. We report that things appear normal. If there is a deviation from normal, you need to document (images) and describe (worksheet) the deviations. We do not diagnose, but provide the information needed for the physician to make the diagnosis. Return to [[option2]] <img src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/74/Electronic_medical_record.jpg"> Before every scan, you should review the patients past medical imaging. This is not only US, but also all modalities. If a patient has past images, you can see what their anatomy looks like and how you can adjust your settings before you even have them on the table. Return to [[option2]] <img src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0e/Prescription_medicine.svg"> With diagnostic medical sonography, we do not put our probe on the patient unless it is medically necessary. You will always verify your scan order with the physicians order before beginning the scan. There are times when what is ordered does not match the physician’s orders and it must be corrected before getting the patient. Return to [[option2]] Now that you are ready for the patient, what is next? [[patient identifier]] [[patient greeting]] [[patient transport]] Now to begin your exam you will go to [[protocols]]You must always check that you have the correct patient. Different facilities have different protocols in place for making sure you have the correct patient. Some use first names, some use last names, and some also use the pager system to maintain patient confidentiality. return to [[option 3]] Patient greetings should be neutral and polite, no slang, or casual jargon. Refer to the patient chart/order on preferred names and pronouns. Return to [[option 3]]Remember to keep patients safe. If your patient struggles with walking, get a wheelchair to assist with the transport to the room. Return to [[option 3]]Every exam has a set protocol of exam order and image presentation. Refer to each clinical site on their image sequence and documentation of anatomy/pathology. We will teach you a basic protocol and it might need to be tweaked a bit from site to site when you are out at clinical. Return to [[option 3]]
